        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">goths, deathers, poppy z. brite fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3236724-private-grave?shelf=2010">2010</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer101808230" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3789865011107743155">Growing up P.Z.B., as a writer, meant so much to me. Her dark, twisted, and aching characters filled my head as if they were people in the real world –stories from a darker part of the world that if I looked hard enough on the fringes of society I could find.<br/><br/>I’m twenty-five now, an old man by my standards, and I find myself rereading P.Z.B. books looking for that key to the darker world. The key to the place where I feel like I truly fit in.<br/><br/>At twenty-five I see P.Z.B.’s characters as childish, y</span>
  <span id="freeText3789865011107743155" style="display:none">Growing up P.Z.B., as a writer, meant so much to me. Her dark, twisted, and aching characters filled my head as if they were people in the real world –stories from a darker part of the world that if I looked hard enough on the fringes of society I could find.<br /><br />I’m twenty-five now, an old man by my standards, and I find myself rereading P.Z.B. books looking for that key to the darker world. The key to the place where I feel like I truly fit in.<br /><br />At twenty-five I see P.Z.B.’s characters as childish, youthful to a fault, achingly trite. The world I once thought was just on the edge of mine is, in fact, not real. It’s a cheap ghost –a movie projected on the wall within my mind. <br /><br />Drawing Blood is the final strands of that ghost being whisked away by time and experience. I feel so little for Trevor and Zach’s tragically opposite gothic personalities. If anything I fell for the other characters in P.Z.B.’s return to Missing Mile, I feel for Kinsey and Terry and the shells of Ghost and Steve because they represent the real world. The supporting characters of Drawing Blood (and to some extent Lost Souls) represent real life. They come to represent the boring, bitter, repetitive world where the magic really doesn’t exist, where the ghosts of my past do not come to haunt me where life isn’t as dark as I want it to be. <br /><br />Drawing Blood takes the haunted house concept and mutates it to a personal story of a haunted past ripe with sex (of all types), drugs, rock and roll and a little bit of (80s) nerdy technology. <br /><br />Read this book if you’re under twenty-five, unafraid of gay sex, and long for a world where we are the lead characters in our own Southern Gothic epic.<br /></span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15412197370633629009">I did not think i could find an horror novel escapist but this was the case with this one; it is my first book by Ms Brite and I found much in it to be pleased about.<br/><br/>The story, if not particularly original, is not worn out and/or dumb. Writing is fairly good and to the point but could be more polished and achieve both more beauty and more tension: from the first page I knew there was going to be a happy ending and as much as I love my endings to be happy I still wish to get more thrills.<br/>I would </span>
  <span id="freeText15412197370633629009" style="display:none">I did not think i could find an horror novel escapist but this was the case with this one; it is my first book by Ms Brite and I found much in it to be pleased about.<br /><br />The story, if not particularly original, is not worn out and/or dumb. Writing is fairly good and to the point but could be more polished and achieve both more beauty and more tension: from the first page I knew there was going to be a happy ending and as much as I love my endings to be happy I still wish to get more thrills.<br />I would not be writing this if I did not believe Ms Brite to have much potential. Some pages are just professional but just as many wield real power: raw and uncouth but thrilling one to the bone with luscious descriptions, meaningful dialogues, clever innuendoes. She just needs more focus.<br /><br />Nominally this is a horror but the author is evidently much more interested in her characters' interaction: they are faceted, interesting, endearing. The side ones are well rounded and believable; the two main ones just adorable: their love grows quickly but convincingly and you feel for them before you know it.<br /><br />There are some sex scenes and they are explicit, graphic, intense: I do not know how a woman could write this well about gay male sex but her sex scenes are perhaps the best parts of the whole novel.<br /><br />The ending is satisfying, it leaves no loose threads and allows one to think "and they lived happily ever after", which is a very good thing.<br /><br />just a short poisonous comment: one of the two main heroes is bisexual... "ms brite, please, be aware that true bisexuality is such a hard thing to find..." </span>

<div id="review_952547988" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/952547988" />
    <a title="Maria Lago" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31845821-maria-lago"><img alt="Maria Lago" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1401465850p2/31845821.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/952547988?book_show_action=true">May 30, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maria Lago" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maria Lago" href="/user/show/31845821-maria-lago">Maria Lago</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31845821-maria-lago?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer952547988" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer467584424871486087">Ok, Brite might have lost his mojo a while ago, according to some, but let us think about when he was everything we needed. He was angsty and sexy and bold and original, and so were his characters, who were wonderfully impossible and wonderfully imperfect. For me, it wasn't like I wanted to be with Zach or Trevor, it's not that I wanted to be them; I just wanted to read about them: pure vouyerism. Their love story is exactly the same as the passionate stories we find in bodice rippers, it's pass</span>
  <span id="freeText467584424871486087" style="display:none">Ok, Brite might have lost his mojo a while ago, according to some, but let us think about when he was everything we needed. He was angsty and sexy and bold and original, and so were his characters, who were wonderfully impossible and wonderfully imperfect. For me, it wasn't like I wanted to be with Zach or Trevor, it's not that I wanted to be them; I just wanted to read about them: pure vouyerism. Their love story is exactly the same as the passionate stories we find in bodice rippers, it's passionate and desperate, it's pure fiction, it's deliberatly as far away from reality as it can get, because, who would want reality when you can fall in love the way these two did?<br />Trevor's character is by far my favourite of Brite's ever. I do not identify with him one iota, but I find him fascinating. I wrote a letter to Brite to tell him how much I loved this book, and Trevor in particular, not expecting him to reply. Imagine how I jumped up and down when I received a parcel that included a handwritten letter and a signed copy of <i>The Lazarous Heart</i>. <br />Come on: Brite was absolutely great and I'm still on his side. But I think it's unfair to expect him to write the same way he used to two decades ago. It was a different time for all of us, and intelligent people change. There was (or there is) something really great in him and his first novels are good proof of it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="467584424871486087" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2877453038" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2877453038" />
    <a title="Devann" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4135942-devann"><img alt="Devann" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603225622p2/4135942.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2877453038?book_show_action=true">Oct 19, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Devann" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Devann" href="/user/show/4135942-devann">Devann</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4135942-devann?shelf=c-dl">c-dl</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4135942-devann?shelf=g-mystery-thriller">g-mystery-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4135942-devann?shelf=g-horror">g-horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4135942-devann?shelf=sg-lgbtia">sg-lgbtia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4135942-devann?shelf=z-19-tower-teams-vii">z-19-tower-teams-vii</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4135942-devann?shelf=2-5-star">2-5-star</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2877453038" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11586520300958674234">actual rating: 2.5<br/><br/>This was ...surprisingly boring for a Poppy Z Brite book. I mean if I'm willing to deal with all the edgy bullshit and misogyny that comes with a PBZ book - although this one *gasp* actually has a woman in it who does not die! or get raped! amazing! - then I'm doing it because I want to read something just super fucked up and this was not that. I know what you're thinking - 'but Devann, it literally starts with a dude murdering his wife and son and then himself' - and yeah that</span>
  <span id="freeText11586520300958674234" style="display:none">actual rating: 2.5<br /><br />This was ...surprisingly boring for a Poppy Z Brite book. I mean if I'm willing to deal with all the edgy bullshit and misogyny that comes with a PBZ book - although this one *gasp* actually has a woman in it who does not die! or get raped! amazing! - then I'm doing it because I want to read something just super fucked up and this was not that. I know what you're thinking - 'but Devann, it literally starts with a dude murdering his wife and son and then himself' - and yeah that was messed up, but that was the prologue and then it was just pretty 'normal' up until towards the end. <br /><br />The stuff where they went to the 'other world' was actually very interesting but that was about the only other part. I mean some of the romance aspect was weirdly cute but I wasn't really looking for cute and I'm kind of disappointed that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[they both actually lived at the end and ran away to some tropical island together <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. But it had good parts and like I said before I'm just shocked that there was a female character who didn't have anything awful happen to her so I rounded up instead of down. <br /><br />Also I do not know why so many people have tagged this 'vampires' because there are literally no vampires anywhere near this. Baffling. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11586520300958674234" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_19488248" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/19488248" />
    <a title="Nicolle Cornute-Sutton" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1056939-nicolle-cornute-sutton"><img alt="Nicolle Cornute-Sutton" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1398228036p2/1056939.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/19488248?book_show_action=true">Apr 04, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicolle Cornute-Sutton" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicolle Cornute-Sutton" href="/user/show/1056939-nicolle-cornute-sutton">Nicolle Cornute-Sutton</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer19488248" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12035576521947145429">This is my favorite of Poppy Brite's books. As the two main characters, Zach and Trevor, fell in love with each other, so I fell in love with them. The horror aspect of the book became an interesting backdrop for the romance.<br/><br/>The prose is a bit on the purple side sure but it's also lush and descriptive and fun, almost but not quite as over the top as say, VC Andrews.<br/><br/>If you like boys who like boys and the supernatural this is the book for you.</span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1490612903" />
    <a title="Varvara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24436119-varvara"><img alt="Varvara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1472374012p2/24436119.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1490612903?book_show_action=true">Jan 02, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Varvara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Varvara" href="/user/show/24436119-varvara">Varvara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780141049472" href="/book/show/8353230-drawing-blood">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24436119-varvara?shelf=read-in-english">read-in-english</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24436119-varvara?shelf=me">me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24436119-varvara?shelf=2016-rereads">2016-rereads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24436119-varvara?shelf=2019">2019</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1490612903" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer161480600340817434">This book feels like a weird, terrifying home to me. I think that this mix of a horror book and a sappy love story is what makes it work so well, bringing me hope of all things. And I love Brite's language; things and phrases I read at 14 are still stuck in my brain, 15 years later %) It probably would have been a very different review if I had read it at 29 for the first time, I guess; but if anything - I'm glad that I hadn't :) </span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1853874849?book_show_action=true">Jan 18, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katriina ❆" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katriina ❆" href="/user/show/13511873-katriina">Katriina ❆</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780140238716" href="/book/show/200384.Drawing_Blood">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13511873-katriina?shelf=in-english">in-english</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13511873-katriina?shelf=in-original-language">in-original-language</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1853874849" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4329711989822348319">Sadly, this book did not make me feel the same things Lost Souls did.<br/>Something was missing, and I do not quite know why. The story was gripping and utterly creative, the characters broken and bent, the prose as flawless as always. Brite has a way of telling stories that has me spiraling down into a writers-depression with every word I read, and still - the book felt incomplete. <br/></span>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('uw/4B7TOh/BFcQ89clOvu8bL9hImKCjT0uXJd/U+2jNgQpo606HD6DICjboGKjVTAsyb5p41w5V/rrRLSz94hw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('CKf0MXLVDHrpXC2edjLBL9vGlc5gSlPYFrbmMO31im/T6pYMFbpIYp4vrxkCS1vHH8H4OthXuJ67/ZsMU/Qo2w==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/9558.Poppy_Z_Brite">About Poppy Z. Brite</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/9558.Poppy_Z_Brite"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1311937607p3/9558.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer8187684683519092163">Poppy Z. Brite (born Melissa Ann Brite, now going by Billy Martin) is an American author born in New Orleans, Louisiana.<br/><br/>Born a biological female, Brite has written and talked much about his gender dysphoria/gender identity issues. He self-identifies almost completely as a homosexual male rather than female, and as of 2011 has started taking testosterone injections. His male name is Billy Martin.<br/><br/>He</span>
  <span id="freeText8187684683519092163" style="display:none">Poppy Z. Brite (born Melissa Ann Brite, now going by Billy Martin) is an American author born in New Orleans, Louisiana.<br /><br />Born a biological female, Brite has written and talked much about his gender dysphoria/gender identity issues. He self-identifies almost completely as a homosexual male rather than female, and as of 2011 has started taking testosterone injections. His male name is Billy Martin.<br /><br />He lived in Chapel Hill, North Carolina and Athens, Georgia prior to returning to New Orleans in 1993. He loves UNC basketball and is a sometime season ticket holder for the NBA, but he saves his greatest affection for his hometown football team, the New Orleans Saints.<br /><br />Brite and husband Chris DeBarr, a chef, run a de facto cat rescue and have, at any given time, between fifteen and twenty cats. Photos of the various felines are available on the "Cats" page of Brite's website. They have been known to have a few dogs and perhaps a snake as well in the menagerie. They are no longer together.<br /><br />During Hurricane Katrina in 2005, Brite at first opted to stay at home, but he eventually abandoned New Orleans and his cats and relocated 80 miles away to his mother's home in Mississippi. He used his blog to update his fans regarding the situation, including the unknown status of his house and many of his pets, and in October 2005 became one of the first 70,000 New Orleanians to begin repopulating the city.<br /><br />In the following months, Brite has been an outspoken and sometimes harsh critic of those who are leaving New Orleans for good. He was quoted in the <i>New York Times</i> and elsewhere as saying, in reference to those considering leaving, "If you’re ever lucky enough to belong somewhere, if a place takes you in and you take it into yourself, you don't desert it just because it can kill you. There are things more valuable than life."</span>
  <a data-text-id="8187684683519092163" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/2510310-drawing-blood">Quotes from Drawing Blood</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Didn’t he have to admit, begrudgingly, that in some extra-perverse corner of his brain the idea of having to be out of town before sundown appealed to him? New Orleans had been the only constant thing in his life. But didn’t he yet an itchy foot sometimes, didn’t he sometimes think about just throwing all his stuff in his car and going?<br />Of course he did. Everybody did, even normal people, the ones with triple mortgages and orthodontists’ bills and responsibilities to everything except what they really wanted.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/596051-didn-t-he-have-to-admit-begrudgingly-that-in-some-extra-perverse">35 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Trevor cupped his hands around it, felt Zach's heartbeat throbbing between his palms. The skin of the shaft was textured, slightly rippled beneath the surface. The head was as smooth as satin, as rose petals. Trevor rubbed his thumb across it, squeezed gently, heard Zack suck air in through his teeth and moan as he let it out. He could see blood suffusing the tissue just beneath the translucent skin, a deep dusky rose delicately purpled at the edges, crowned with a single dewy pearl of come. It was as intimate, as raw as holding someone's heart in his hands.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/1239639-trevor-cupped-his-hands-around-it-felt-zach-s-heartbeat-throbbing">34 likes</a>
